<ul><li>Apple</li><li>Banana</li><li>Cherry</li></ul> displays a bullet list of fruits.

<ul><li>Frontend</li><li>Backend<ul><li>Node.js</li><li>Python</li></ul></li></ul> demonstrates nesting. ^5hKaiNwf

Parent: <ul>

Children: one or more <li> elements

Attributes (optional): type (deprecated), class, id, style, aria-* for accessibility ^uuliQlAY

Using non-<li> children inside <ul>, which violates HTML spec.

Styling list bullets manually without removing default browser styles first.

Assuming screen readers interpret list semantics when ARIA roles are absent or misused. ^pcr8EFYw

VS <ol>: <ul> implies no order; <ol> is for ordered/numbered sequences.

VS <dl>: <dl> is used for name-value pairs, not lists of items. ^z9VCLCtb

An unordered list in HTML is a semantic element used to group related items without implying a specific order or sequence. It is defined using the <ul> tag, which encloses a collection of <li> (list item) elements.Browsers render unordered lists by default with bullets, but presentation can be altered via CSS. 
Nesting of <ul> elements is valid and allows for the creation of hierarchical list structures. ^T5eckakS
